# End-to-End: How Kubernetes Creates a Deployment

## Your Task

You are onboarding to the Kubernetes project. A senior engineer has asked you to produce
a technical explanation of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created — tracing the full
request flow from a client application through the API server and into persistent storage.

**Your question**: Explain how a Kubernetes client application creates a Deployment from
start to finish. Your explanation must trace through all three layers:

1. **Client library** — What type/function in `kubernetes-client-go` sends the HTTP request?
2. **API server** — What function in `kubernetes/kubernetes` receives and validates the create request?
3. **Storage** — What function in `etcd-io/etcd` persists the Deployment to the key-value store?

For each step, cite the specific repository, file path, and function/type name.

## Context

You are working in a Kubernetes ecosystem with the following repos:

- `kubernetes/kubernetes` (the core orchestrator)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (go-client-library)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-api` (api-type-definitions)
- `etcd-io/etcd` (distributed-kv-store)

This question is specifically designed to benefit from cross-repo synthesis. Use your
search tools to trace the full path across repositories.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "chain": [
    {
      "repo": "sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go",
      "path": "relative/path/to/file.go",
      "symbol": "FunctionOrTypeName",
      "description": "What this step does in the flow"
    }
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive narrative explaining the end-to-end flow, citing specific files and functions from each repo."
}
```

**Important**: Use the exact repo identifiers specified for this task. The oracle expects `repo` values of `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (client layer), `kubernetes/kubernetes` (API server layer), and `etcd-io/etcd` (storage layer). The `repo` field must match these exactly.
**Note**: Tool output may return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`). Strip this prefix in your answer — use `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, NOT `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`.

The `chain` should contain at least 3 steps representing the 3 layers described above.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **Flow coverage**: Does the chain include key steps from all 3 layers (client → server → storage)?
- **Technical accuracy**: Are the cited file paths and function names correct?
- **Provenance**: Does your narrative reference all three repositories?
- **Synthesis quality** (supplementary): Does the explanation connect the layers clearly?

     1→# Create, Update & Delete Deployment
     2→
     3→This example program demonstrates the fundamental operations for managing on
     4→[Deployment][1] resources, such as `Create`, `List`, `Update` and `Delete`.
     5→
     6→You can adopt the source code from this example to write programs that manage
     7→other types of resources through the Kubernetes API.
     8→
     9→## Running this example
    10→
    11→Make sure you have a Kubernetes cluster and `kubectl` is configured:
    12→
    13→    kubectl get nodes
    14→
    15→Compile this example on your workstation:
    16→
    17→```
    18→cd create-update-delete-deployment
    19→go build -o ./app
    20→```
    21→
    22→Now, run this application on your workstation with your local kubeconfig file:
    23→
    24→```
    25→./app
    26→# or specify a kubeconfig file with flag
    27→./app -kubeconfig=$HOME/.kube/config
    28→```
    29→
    30→Running this command will execute the following operations on your cluster:
    31→
    32→1. **Create Deployment:** This will create a 2 replica Deployment. Verify with
    33→   `kubectl get pods`.
    34→2. **Update Deployment:** This will update the Deployment resource created in
    35→   previous step by setting the replica count to 1 and changing the container
    36→   image to `nginx:1.13`. You are encouraged to inspect the retry loop that
    37→   handles conflicts. Verify the new replica count and container image with
    38→   `kubectl describe deployment demo`.
    39→3. **List Deployments:** This will retrieve Deployments in the `default`
    40→   namespace and print their names and replica counts.
    41→4. **Delete Deployment:** This will delete the Deployment object and its
    42→   dependent ReplicaSet resource. Verify with `kubectl get 
... (truncated)

## Summary: Creating Kubernetes Deployments in kubernetes-client-go

Based on my search of the sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go repository, here is how client applications create Deployments:

### 1. **How a Client Application Creates a Deployment**

Client applications follow this pattern (from `/workspace/client-go/examples/create-update-delete-deployment/main.go`, lines 63-107):

```go
// Get the Deployments client for a specific namespace
deploymentsClient := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(apiv1.NamespaceDefault)

// Create a Deployment object
deployment := &appsv1.Deployment{
    ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{
        Name: "demo-deployment",
    },
    Spec: appsv1.DeploymentSpec{
        Replicas: int32Ptr(2),
        // ... rest of spec
    },
}

// Call Create to send it to the Kubernetes API server
result, err := deploymentsClient.Create(context.TODO(), deployment, metav1.CreateOptions{})
```

**File:** `/workspace/client-go/gentype/type.go`

		UseProtobufAsDefaultIfPreferred(c.prefersProtobuf).
		NamespaceIfScoped(c.namespace, c.namespace != "").
		Resource(c.resource).                                   // "deployments"
		VersionedParams(&opts, c.paramet

   251→
   252→// GetResourceKind returns the external group version kind registered for the given storage
   253→// object. If the storage object is a subresource and has an override supplied for it, it returns
   254→// the group version kind supplied in the override.
   255→func GetResourceKind(groupVersion schema.GroupVersion, storage rest.Storage, typer runtime.ObjectTyper) (schema.GroupVersionKind, error) {
   256→	// Let the storage tell us exactly what GVK it has
   257→	if gvkProvider, ok := storage.(rest.GroupVersionKindProvider); ok {
   258→		return gvkProvider.GroupVersionKind(groupVersion), nil
   259→	}
   260→
   261→	object := storage.New()
   262→	fqKinds, _, err := typer.ObjectKinds(object)
   263→	if err != nil {
   264→		return schema.GroupVersionKind{}, err
   265→	}
   266→
   267→	// a given go type can have multiple potential fully qualified kinds.  Find the one that corresponds with the group
   268→	// we're trying to register here
   269→	fqKindToRegister := schema.GroupVersionKind{}
   270→	for _, fqKind := range fqKinds {
   271→		if fqKind.Group == groupVersion.Group {
   272→			fqKindToRegister = groupVersion.WithKind(fqKind.Kind)
   273→			break
   274→		}
   275→	}
   276→	if fqKindToRegister.Empty() {
   277→		return schema.GroupVersionKind{}, fmt.Errorf("unable to locate fully qualified kind for %v: found %v when registering for %v", reflect.TypeOf(object), fqKinds, groupVersion)
   278→	}
   279→
   280→	// group is guaranteed to match based on the check above
   281→	return fqKindToRegister, nil
   282→}

```go
func (e *Store) create(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object, ...) (runtime.Object, error) {
    // ... validation and preparation ...
    key, err := e.KeyFunc(ctx, name)
    ttl, err := e.calculateTTL(obj, 0, false)
    out := e.NewFunc()
    if err := e.Storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, out, ttl, ...); err != nil {
        // ... error handling ...
    }
    return out, nil
}
```

The `Store.Create()` method in etcd3 storage encodes the object and sends it to etcd:

func (s *store) Create(ctx context.Context, key string, obj, out runtime.Object, ttl uint64) error {
    preparedKey, err := s.prepareKey(key)
    // Encode the object to bytes
    data, err := runtime.Encode(s.codec, obj)
    
    // Transform data for encryption/compression if needed
    newData, err := s.transformer.TransformToStorage(ctx, data, ...)
    
    // Call OptimisticPut on the etcd client
    txnResp, err := s.client.Kubernetes.OptimisticPut(ctx, preparedKey, newData, 0, kubernetes.PutOptions{LeaseID: lease})

232-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer tracing the complete flow of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created across all three layers. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary: End-to-End Deployment Creation

### **Layer 1: Client Library** (sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go)
- **Function**: `Client[T].Create()` in `client-go/gentype/type.go:243-255`
- **Action**: Sends HTTP POST request with serialized Deployment to `/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments`

### **Layer 2: API Server** (kubernetes/kubernetes)
Multiple steps:
1. **`createHandler()`** in `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:53-236`: Receives HTTP POST, decodes body, validates CreateOptions
2. **`Store.Create()`** in `pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:446-558`: Validates Deployment structure, clears status field, sets Generation=1, runs admission, delegates to etcd
3. **etcd3 storage adapter** in `pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`: Encodes object, transforms for encryption, sends OptimisticPut to etcd

### **Layer 3: Storage Backend** (etcd-io/etcd)
Multiple steps:
1. **RAFT consensus**: Replicates entry across cluster
2. **`applierV3backend.Put()`** in `server/etcdserver/apply.go:249-302`: Applies committed entry to MVCC store
3. **`storeTxnWrite.Put()`** in `server/mvcc/kvstore_txn.go:109-112`: Marshals KeyValue protobuf, writes to batch transaction
4. **`batchTx.Commit()`** in `server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go:261-288`: Flushes to BOLT database, fsync to disk

The complete answer with detailed narrative, code snippets, and all citations has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`.

The Create method constructs an HTTP POST request using a REST client:\\n\\n```go\\nerr := c.client.Post().\\n    Resource(c.resource).           // \\\"deployments\\\"\\n `/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`.\\n\\n### Layer 2: API Server (kubernetes/kubernetes)\\n\\nThe Kubernetes API server receives the HTTP POST request through its REST API handler chain.\\n\\n**Step 1: HTTP Handler** \u2014 The `createHandler` function in `kubernetes/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:53-236` is invoked:\\n\\n- Parses the request namespace and resource name from the URL\\n- Negotiates the content type (JSON, YAML, or protobuf)\\n- Reads and decodes the request body into a Deployment object\\n- Parses CreateOptions from query parameters\\n- Validates the request structure\\n\\n**Step 2: Storage Layer Delegation** \u2014 At line 184-190 of create.go, the handler calls:\\n\\n```go\\nreturn r.Create(\\n    ctx,\\n    name,\\n    obj,\\n    rest.AdmissionToValidateObjectFunc(admit, admissionAttributes, scope),\\n    options,\\n)\\n```\\n\\nThis delegates to the generic storage registry's Create method.\\n\\n**Step 3: Generic Storage Registry** \u2014 The `Store.Create` method in `kubernetes/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:446-558` performs the core validation and preparation:\\n\\n- Initializes object metadata using `FillObjectMetaSystemFields` (sets UID, creation timestamp, etc.)\\n- If the Deployment uses GenerateName, generates a unique name and sets it\\n- Calls the Deployment's PrepareForCreate strategy hook (in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/strategy.go`), which:\\n  - Clears the Status field (status is maintained by controllers, not stored during creation)\\n  - Sets Generation to 1\\n  - Drops any disabled template fields\\n- Runs Validate() to check the Deployment spec is valid\\n- Runs admission webhooks to validate or mutate the object\\n- Calls the etcd3 storage backend's Create method at line 526:\\n\\n```go\\nerr := e.Storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, out, ttl, ...)\\n```\\n\\n### Layer 3: Persistent Storage (etcd-io/etcd)\\n\\nThe etcd3 storage adapter and etcd server work together to durably persist the Deployment.\\n\\n**Step 1: etcd3 Storage Backend** \u2014 The `store.Create` method in the etcd3 adapter (`kubernetes/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`) encodes and sends the Deployment to etcd:\\n\\n- Encodes the Deployment object to bytes using the codec (typically protobuf)\\n- Transforms the data for encryption or compression if configured\\n- Sends an OptimisticPut request to the etcd client with the encoded data\\n- The etcd client wraps this in a conditional transaction checking the key's modRevision\\n\\n**Step 2: RAFT Consensus** \u2014 The etcd server receives the Put request and:\\n\\n- Wraps it in a RAFT log entry in `server/etcdserver/v3_server.go`\\n- Uses RAFT consensus to replicate the entry across the cluster (leader + followers)\\n- Once a majority acknowledges, the entry is marked as committed\\n\\n**Step 3: Apply Committed Entry** \u2014 The apply loop in `server/etcdserver/apply.go` processes the committed RAFT entry:\\n\\n- Extracts the Put request from the RAFT entry\\n- Invokes the `applierV3backend.Put` method (lines 249-302) to apply to the MVCC store\\n- Creates an MVCC write transaction\\n- Calls `txn.Put(key, value, leaseID)` to add the Deployment to the transaction\\n\\n**Step 4: MVCC Transaction Persistence** \u2014 The `storeTxnWrite.Put` method in `server/mvcc/kvstore_txn.go:109-112` marshals the KeyValue protobuf:\\n\\n- Constructs an `mvccpb.KeyValue` protobuf message containing:\\n  - `key`: The deployment key (e.g., \\\"/deployments/default/my-deployment\\\")\\n  - `value`: The serialized Deployment object\\n  - `createRevision`: The MVCC revision when first created\\n  - `modRevision`: The current revision\\n  - `version`: Incremented on each modification\\n  - `lease`: Associated lease ID (for TTL, if any)\\n- Marshals the protobuf to bytes using `kv.Marshal()`\\n- Calls `UnsafeSeqPut` (line 226) to write the serialized bytes to the backend batch transaction:\\n\\n```go\\ntw.tx.UnsafeSeqPut(buckets.Key, ibytes, d)\\n```\\n\\n**Step 5: Batch Transaction Commit** \u2014 After all committed RAFT entries have been applied, the batch transaction is committed in `server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go:261-288`:\\n\\n- The `batchTx.Commit()` method flushes all pending writes from the in-memory buffer\\n- Calls `t.tx.Commit()` to commit the BOLT database transaction (line 273)\\n- BOLT writes the data to the memory-mapped database file (typically `/var/lib/etcd/member/snap/db`)\\n- BOLT performs an fsync system call to ensure the bytes are durably written to disk\\n\\nOnce this fsync completes, the Deployment is guaranteed to be persisted, even in the face of power loss or system failure.\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\nThe complete flow is:\\n\\n```\\nClient App\\n  \u2193\\nsg-evals/kubernetes-client-go: Client[T].Create() \u2014 HTTP POST request\\n  \u2193\\nkubernetes/kubernetes: createHandler() \u2014 Receive and decode\\n  \u2193\\nkubernetes/kubernetes: Store.Create() \u2014 Validate and prepare\\n  \u2193\\netcd-io/etcd: RAFT consensus \u2014 Replicate entry\\n  \u2193\\netcd-io/etcd: applierV3backend.Put() \u2014 Apply to MVCC\\n  \u2193\\netcd-io/etcd: storeTxnWrite.Put() \u2014 Marshal protobuf\\n  \u2193\\netcd-io/etcd: batchTx.Commit() \u2014 Persist to BOLT disk\\n  \u2193\\nDurable Storage (BOLT database file)\\n```\\n\\nEach layer has a clear responsibility: the client sends the request, the API server validates it according to Kubernetes semantics, and etcd handles replication and durable persistence. The separation of concerns ensures that Deployments are reliably created and stored across the distributed Kubernetes system.\"\n}\n",
